\xe3\x84\x90\xe3\x84\xa7\xe3\x84\xa3 \xe3\x84\x96\xe3\x84\xa8\xe3\x84\xa5\xcb\x8a \xe3\x84\x93\xe3\x84\xa8\xe3\x84\xa5 \xe3\x84\x92\xe3\x84\xa7\xe3\x84\xa3\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;">\n            <a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles" title="Wade\xe2\x80\x93Giles">\n             Wade\xe2\x80\x93Giles\n            </a>\n  Tongyong Pinyin\n            </a>\n           </th>\n           <td>\n            t\xc3\xa1i b\xc4\x9bi gu\xc3\xb3 j\xc3\xac jin r\xc3\xb3ng jhong sin\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n         </table>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="display:none">\n        <td colspan="2">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Taipei 101\n       </b>\n       /\n       <b>\n        TAIPEI 101\n       </b>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skyscraperCenter_1-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-skyscraperCenter-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , formerly known as the\n       <b>\n        Taipei World Financial Center\n       </b>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Landmark" title="Landmark">\n        landmark\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skyscrapers" title="Skyscrapers">\n        supertall skyscraper\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xinyi_District" title="Xinyi District">\n        Xinyi District\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">\n        Taipei\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">\n        Taiwan\n       </a>\n       . The building was officially classified as the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings" title="List of tallest buildings">\n        world\'s tallest\n       </a>\n       in 2004, and remained such until the completion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">\n        Burj Khalifa\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">\n        Dubai\n       </a>\n       in 2010. In 2011, the building was awarded the LEED platinum certification, the highest award according to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">\n        Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design\n       </a>\n       (LEED) rating system, and became the tallest and largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Green_building" title="Green building">\n        green building\n       </a>\n       in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FTleed_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FTleed-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STleed_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-STleed-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It used to have the fastest elevator in the world, traveling at 60.6\xc2\xa0km/h and transporting passengers from the 5th to 89th floor in 37 seconds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2016, the title for the fastest elevator was given to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Tower" title="Shanghai Tower">\n        Shanghai Tower\n       </a>\n       in Shanghai, China.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Construction on the 101-story tower started in 1999 and finished in 2004. The tower has served as an icon of modern Taiwan ever since its opening. The building was\n       <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">\n        architecturally\n       </a>\n       created as a\n       <a href="#Symbolism">\n        symbol\n       </a>\n       of the evolution of technology and Asian tradition. Its\n       <a href="/wiki/Postmodernism" title="Postmodernism">\n        postmodernist\n       </a>\n       approach to style incorporates traditional design elements and gives them modern treatments. The tower is designed to withstand\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">\n        typhoons\n       </a>\n       and earthquakes. A multi-level shopping mall adjoining the tower houses hundreds of stores, restaurants and clubs.\n       <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">\n        Fireworks\n       </a>\n       launched from Taipei 101 feature prominently in international New Year\'s Eve broadcasts and the structure appears frequently in travel literature and international media.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 is owned by\n       <a href="/wiki/Taipei_Financial_Center_Corporation" title="Taipei Financial Center Corporation">\n        Taipei Financial Center Corporation\n       </a>\n       . The name that was originally planned for the building, Taipei World Financial Center, until 2003, was derived from the name of the owner.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Features">\n <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#Construction">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Construction\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n           <a href="#Chronology">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n      <a href="#Events">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Events\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#New_Year.27s_Eve_fireworks_displays">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             New Year\'s Eve fireworks displays\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Developments">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Developments\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">\n        Features\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Height">\n        Height\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Height">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_base.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Taipei_101_base.jpg/250px-Taipei_101_base.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Taipei_101_base.jpg/375px-Taipei_101_base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Taipei_101_base.jpg/500px-Taipei_101_base.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_base.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Base of the tower\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 comprises 101 floors above ground, as well as 5 basement levels. It was not only the first building in the world to break the half-kilometer mark in height,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_3-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emporis-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but also the world\'s tallest building from March 2004 to 10 March 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of 28 July 2011\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , it is still the world\'s largest and highest-use green building.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FTleed_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FTleed-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STleed_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-STleed-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Upon its completion, Taipei 101 was the world\'s tallest inhabited building, at 509.2\xc2\xa0m (1,671\xc2\xa0ft) as measured to its height architectural top (\n       <a href="/wiki/Spire" title="Spire">\n        spire\n       </a>\n       ), exceeding the\n       <a href="/wiki/Petronas_Towers" title="Petronas Towers">\n        Petronas Towers\n       </a>\n       , which were previously the tallest inhabited skyscraper at 451.9\xc2\xa0m (1,483\xc2\xa0ft). The height to the top of the roof, at 449.2\xc2\xa0m (1,474\xc2\xa0ft), and highest occupied floor, at 439.2\xc2\xa0m (1,441\xc2\xa0ft), surpassed the previous records of 442\xc2\xa0m (1,450\xc2\xa0ft) and 412.4\xc2\xa0m (1,353\xc2\xa0ft), respectively; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Willis_Tower" title="Willis Tower">\n        Willis Tower\n       </a>\n       had previously held that distinction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_3-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emporis-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-criteria_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-criteria-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-change_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-change-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It also surpassed the 85-story, 347.5\xc2\xa0m (1,140\xc2\xa0ft)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuntex_Sky_Tower" title="Tuntex Sky Tower">\n        Tuntex Sky Tower\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kaohsiung" title="Kaohsiung">\n        Kaohsiung\n       </a>\n       as the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Taiwan" title="List of tallest buildings in Taiwan">\n        tallest building in Taiwan\n       </a>\n       and the 51-story, 244.15\xc2\xa0m (801\xc2\xa0ft)\n       <a href="/wiki/Shin_Kong_Life_Tower" title="Shin Kong Life Tower">\n        Shin Kong Life Tower\n       </a>\n       as the tallest building in Taipei.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DIT_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DIT-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Taipei 101 claimed the official records for the world\'s tallest\n       <a href="/wiki/Sundial" title="Sundial">\n        sundial\n       </a>\n       and the world\'s largest\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year\'s Eve">\n        New Year\'s Eve\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Countdown_clock" title="Countdown clock">\n        countdown clock\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CP_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CP-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Various sources, including the building\'s owners, give the height of Taipei 101 as 508\xc2\xa0m (1,667\xc2\xa0ft), roof height and top floor height as 448\xc2\xa0m (1,470\xc2\xa0ft) and 438\xc2\xa0m (1,437\xc2\xa0ft). This lower figure is derived by measuring from the top of a 1.2\xc2\xa0m (4\xc2\xa0ft) platform at the base.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skyscraperCenter_1-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-skyscraperCenter-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_3-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emporis-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       CTBUH standards, though, include the height of the platform in calculating the overall height, as it represents part of the man-made structure and is above the level of the surrounding pavement.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-criteria_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-criteria-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-change_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-change-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP_20-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Taipei 101 displaced the Petronas Towers as the tallest building in the world by 57.3\xc2\xa0m (188\xc2\xa0ft).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_19-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The record it claimed for greatest height from ground to\n       <a href="/wiki/Pinnacle" title="Pinnacle">\n        pinnacle\n       </a>\n       was surpassed by the Burj Khalifa in Dubai, which is 829.8\xc2\xa0m (2,722\xc2\xa0ft) in height. Taipei 101\'s records for roof height and highest occupied floor briefly passed to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_World_Financial_Center" title="Shanghai World Financial Center">\n        Shanghai World Financial Center\n       </a>\n       in 2008, which in turn yielded these records as well to the Burj.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-criteria_17-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-criteria-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_19-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-history-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_design">\n        Structural design\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Structural design">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg/200px-Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg/300px-Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg/400px-Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper_2010.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="769" data-file-width="922" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png/200px-Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png/300px-Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png/400px-Taipei_101_Tuned_Mass_Damper.png 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Location of Taipei 101\'s largest\n          <a href="/wiki/Tuned_mass_damper" title="Tuned mass damper">\n           tuned mass damper\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg/200px-Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg/300px-Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg/400px-Tuned_mass_damper_-_Taipei_101_-_Wikimania_2007_0224.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Tuned mass damper\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 is designed to withstand the\n       <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">\n        typhoon\n       </a>\n       winds and earthquake tremors that are common in the area east of Taiwan. Evergreen Consulting Engineering, the structural engineer, designed Taipei 101 to withstand gale winds of 60 metres per second (197\xc2\xa0ft/s), (216\xc2\xa0km/h or 134\xc2\xa0mph), as well as the strongest earthquakes in a 2,500-year cycle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brochure_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-brochure-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 was designed to be flexible as well as structurally resistant, because while flexibility prevents structural damage, resistance ensures comfort for the occupants and for the protection of glass,\n       <a href="/wiki/Curtain_wall_(architecture)" title="Curtain wall (architecture)">\n        curtain walls\n       </a>\n       , and other features.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taipei101-features_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-taipei101-features-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Most designs achieve the necessary strength by enlarging critical structural elements such as bracing. Because of the height of Taipei 101, combined with the surrounding area\'s geology\xe2\x80\x94the building is located just 660\xc2\xa0ft (200\xc2\xa0m) away from a major fault line\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       \xe2\x80\x94Taipei 101 used high-performance steel construction and 36 columns, including eight "mega-columns" packed with 10,000\xc2\xa0psi (69\xc2\xa0MPa) concrete.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floor89PPM_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Floor89PPM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Outrigger trusses, located at eight-floor intervals, connect the columns in the building\'s core to those on the exterior.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SED_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SED-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       These features, combined with the solidity of its\n       <a href="/wiki/Foundation_(engineering)" title="Foundation (engineering)">\n        foundation\n       </a>\n       , made Taipei 101 one of the most stable buildings ever constructed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The foundation is reinforced by 380 piles driven 80\xc2\xa0m (262\xc2\xa0ft) into the ground, extending as far as 30\xc2\xa0m (98\xc2\xa0ft) into the bedrock. Each pile is 1.5\xc2\xa0m (5\xc2\xa0ft) in diameter and can bear a load of 1,000\xe2\x80\x931,320\n       <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">\n        tonnes\n       </a>\n       (1,100\xe2\x80\x931,460\n       <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">\n        short tons\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floor89PPM_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Floor89PPM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During construction, on 31 March 2002, a 6.8-magnitude earthquake rocked Taipei; two construction cranes from the 56th floor, the highest floor at the time, toppled. Five people died in the accident, but an inspection showed no structural damage to the building, and construction soon resumed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SED_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SED-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/RWDI" title="RWDI">\n        RWDI\n       </a>\n       designed a 660-tonne (728-short-ton)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       steel pendulum that serves as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuned_mass_damper" title="Tuned mass damper">\n        tuned mass damper\n       </a>\n       , at a cost of NT$132\xc2\xa0million (US$4\xc2\xa0million).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMD_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TMD-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Suspended from the 92nd to the 87th floor, the pendulum sways to offset movements in the building caused by strong gusts. Its sphere, the largest damper sphere in the world, consists of 41 circular steel plates of varying diameters, each 125\xc2\xa0mm (4.92\xc2\xa0in) thick, welded together to form a 5.5\xc2\xa0m (18\xc2\xa0ft) diameter sphere. Two additional tuned mass dampers, each weighing 6 tonnes (7 short tons), are installed at the tip of the spire which help prevent damage to the structure due to strong wind loads.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMD_34-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TMD-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 8 August 2015, strong winds from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Soudelor_(2015)" title="Typhoon Soudelor (2015)">\n        Typhoon Soudelor\n       </a>\n       swayed the main damper by 100 centimetres (39\xc2\xa0in)\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x93 the largest movement ever recorded by the damper.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The damper has become such a popular tourist attraction, the city contracted\n       <a href="/wiki/Sanrio" title="Sanrio">\n        Sanrio\n       </a>\n       to create a mascot: the Damper Baby. Four versions of the Damper Baby: "Rich Gold", "Cool Black", "Smart Silver" and "Lucky Red" were designed and made into figurines and souvenirs sold in various Taipei 101 gift shops. Damper Baby, with its cute all-ages appeal, has become a popular local icon, with its own comic book and website.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Binder_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Binder-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Structural_fa\xc3\xa7ade">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Structural_fa.C3.A7ade">\n        Structural fa\xc3\xa7ade\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Structural fa\xc3\xa7ade">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:179px;max-width:179px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="587" data-file-width="700" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg/175px-101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg/263px-101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg/350px-101.typhoon.altonthompson.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Taipei 101 during a\n          <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">\n           typhoon\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:101.tall.altonthompson.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="713" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/101.tall.altonthompson.jpg/175px-101.tall.altonthompson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/101.tall.altonthompson.jpg/263px-101.tall.altonthompson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/101.tall.altonthompson.jpg/350px-101.tall.altonthompson.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          View from the base of the tower, looking up\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="518" data-file-width="500" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg/175px-Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg/263px-Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg/350px-Taipei.101.ruyi.altonthompson.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          <a href="/wiki/Ruyi_(scepter)" title="Ruyi (scepter)">\n           Ruyi\n          </a>\n          figure over one of the building\'s entrances\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei101.Sundial.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="3008" data-file-width="1935" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Taipei101.Sundial.jpg/175px-Taipei101.Sundial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Taipei101.Sundial.jpg/263px-Taipei101.Sundial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Taipei101.Sundial.jpg/350px-Taipei101.Sundial.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Shadow of the tower in the late afternoon; the adjoining park (circular feature, bottom) acts as the face of a\n          <a href="/wiki/Sundial" title="Sundial">\n           sundial\n          </a>\n          .\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:177px;max-width:177px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="479" data-file-width="1000" height="84" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg/175px-Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg/263px-Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg/350px-Taipei.101.fountain.altonthompson.jpg 2x" width="175"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          <i>\n           <a href="/wiki/Feng_shui" title="Feng shui">\n            Feng shui\n           </a>\n          </i>\n          fountain outside Taipei 101\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101\'s characteristic blue-green glass curtain walls are double paned and glazed, offer heat and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UV" title="UV">\n        UV\n       </a>\n       protection sufficient to block external heat by 50 percent, and can sustain impacts of 7 tonnes (8 short tons).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brochure_25-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-brochure-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The fa\xc3\xa7ade system of glass and aluminum panels installed into an inclined moment-resisting lattices contributes to overall lateral rigidity by tying back to the mega-columns with one-story high trusses at every eighth floor. This fa\xc3\xa7ade system is therefore able to withstand up to 95\xc2\xa0mm (4\xc2\xa0in) of seismic lateral displacements without damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The original corners of the fa\xc3\xa7ade were tested at\n       <a href="/wiki/RWDI" title="RWDI">\n        RWDI\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">\n        Ontario\n       </a>\n       . A simulation of a 100-year storm at RWDI revealed a vortex that formed during a 3-second 105 miles per hour (169\xc2\xa0km/h) wind at a height of 10 meters, or equivalent to the lateral tower sway rate causing large\n       <a href="/wiki/Crosswind" title="Crosswind">\n        crosswind\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oscillations" title="Oscillations">\n        oscillations\n       </a>\n       . A double chamfered step design was found to dramatically reduce this crosswind oscillation, resulting in the final design\'s "double stairstep" corner fa\xc3\xa7ade.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SnarkyNomad_2013_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SnarkyNomad_2013-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Architect C.Y. Lee also used extensive fa\xc3\xa7ade elements to represent the symbolic identity he pursued. These fa\xc3\xa7ade elements included the green tinted glass for the indigenous slender bamboo look, eight upper outwards inclined tiers of pagoda each with eight floors, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Ruyi_(scepter)" title="Ruyi (scepter)">\n        Ruyi\n       </a>\n       and a money box symbol between the two fa\xc3\xa7ade sections among others.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101\'s own roof and fa\xc3\xa7ade recycled water system meets 20 to 30 percent of the building\'s water needs. In July 2011, Taipei 101 was certified "the world\'s tallest green building" under\n       <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">\n        LEED\n       </a>\n       standards.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Symbolism">\n        Symbolism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Symbolism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg/300px-Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg/450px-Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg/600px-Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_from_afar.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Taipei 101 in the skyline.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The height of 101 floors commemorates the renewal of time: the new century that arrived as the tower was built (100+1) and all the new years that follow (1 January = 1-01). It symbolizes high ideals by going one better on 100, a traditional number of perfection. The number also evokes the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binary_numeral_system" title="Binary numeral system">\n        binary numeral system\n       </a>\n       used in digital technology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floor89PPM_28-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Floor89PPM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The main tower features a series of eight segments of eight floors each. In Chinese-speaking cultures the number\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/8_(number)" title="8 (number)">\n        eight\n       </a>\n       is associated with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Numbers_in_Chinese_culture" title="Numbers in Chinese culture">\n        abundance, prosperity and good fortune\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSnumber_45-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FSnumber-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The repeated segments simultaneously recall the rhythms of an Asian\n       <a href="/wiki/Pagoda" title="Pagoda">\n        pagoda\n       </a>\n       (a tower linking earth and sky, also evoked in the Petronas Towers), a stalk of\n       <a href="/wiki/Bamboo" title="Bamboo">\n        bamboo\n       </a>\n       (an icon of learning and growth), and a stack of ancient Chinese ingots or money boxes (a symbol of abundance). Popular humor sometimes likens the building\'s shape to a stack of\n       <a href="/wiki/Oyster_pail" title="Oyster pail">\n        take-out boxes\n       </a>\n       as used in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Chinese_food" title="American Chinese food">\n        Western-style Chinese food\n       </a>\n       ; of course, the stackable shape of such boxes is likewise derived from that of ancient money boxes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The four discs mounted on each face of the building where the pedestal meets the tower represent coins. The emblem placed over entrances shows three gold coins of ancient design with central holes shaped to imply the\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_numerals" title="Arabic numerals">\n        Arabic numerals\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        1-0-1\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floor89PPM_28-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Floor89PPM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The structure incorporates many shapes of squares and circles to reach a balance between yin and yang.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Curled ruyi figures appear throughout the structure as a design\n       <a href="/wiki/Motif_(visual_arts)" title="Motif (visual arts)">\n        motif\n       </a>\n       . Though the shape of each ruyi at Taipei 101 is traditional, its rendering in industrial metal is plainly modern. The ruyi is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Talisman" title="Talisman">\n        talisman\n       </a>\n       of ancient origin associated in art with\n       <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">\n        heavenly clouds\n       </a>\n       . It connotes healing, protection and fulfillment. It appears in celebrations of the attainment of new career heights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internet_Archive_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Internet_Archive-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The sweeping curved roof of the adjoining mall culminates in a colossal ruyi that shades pedestrians.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internet_Archive_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Internet_Archive-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Each ruyi ornament on the exterior of the Taipei 101 tower stands at least 8\xc2\xa0m (26\xc2\xa0ft) tall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At night the bright yellow gleam from its pinnacle casts Taipei 101 in the role of a candle or\n       <a href="/wiki/Torch" title="Torch">\n        torch\n       </a>\n       upholding the ideals of liberty and welcome. From 6:00 to 10:00 each evening\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the tower\'s lights display one of seven colours in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spectrum" title="Spectrum">\n        spectrum\n       </a>\n       . The colors coincide with the days of the week:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:1em auto;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Day\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Monday\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Tuesday\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Wednesday\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Thursday\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Friday\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Saturday\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Sunday\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Color\n        </th>\n        <td style="background:red; color:white">\n         red\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:orange; color:white">\n         orange\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:gold; color:white">\n         yellow\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:green; color:white">\n         green\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:blue; color:white">\n         blue\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:violet; color:white">\n         violet\n        </td>\n        <td style="background:purple; color:white">\n         purple\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The adjoining Taipei 101 on the east side connects the landmark further with the symbolism of time. The design of the circular park doubles as the face of a giant\n       <a href="/wiki/Sundial" title="Sundial">\n        sundial\n       </a>\n       . The tower itself casts the shadow to mark afternoon hours for the building\'s occupants. The park\'s design is echoed in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Clock" title="Clock">\n        clock\n       </a>\n       that stands at its entrance. The clock runs on\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">\n        energy\n       </a>\n       drawn from the building\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">\n        wind shear\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101, like many of its neighbours, shows the influence of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Feng_shui" title="Feng shui">\n         feng shui\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       philosophy. An example appears in the form of a large granite fountain at the intersection of Songlian Road and Xinyi Road near the tower\'s east entrance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A ball at the fountain\'s top spins toward the tower. As a work of public art the fountain offers a contrast to the tower in texture even as its design echoes the tower\'s rhythms. The fountain also serves a practical function in\n       <i>\n        feng shui\n       </i>\n       philosophy. A\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       intersection near the entrance of a building represents a potential drain of positive energy, or\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Qi" title="Qi">\n         ch\'i\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , from a structure and its occupants.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Placing flowing water at such spots is thought to help redirect the flow of\n       <i>\n        ch\'i\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FS_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FS-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Interior">\n        Interior\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Interior">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 is the first record-setting skyscraper to be constructed in the 21st century. It exhibits a number of technologically advanced features as it provides a center for business and recreation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_3-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emporis-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The original 2004\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiber-optic" title="Fiber-optic">\n        fiber-optic\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Internet_access" title="Satellite Internet access">\n        satellite Internet\n       </a>\n       connections permitted transfer speeds up to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Gigabit" title="Gigabit">\n        gigabit\n       </a>\n       per second.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taipei101-features_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-taipei101-features-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Double-deck_elevator" title="Double-deck elevator">\n        double-deck elevators\n       </a>\n       built by the Japanese\n       <a href="/wiki/Toshiba" title="Toshiba">\n        Toshiba\n       </a>\n       Elevator and Building Systems Corporation (TELC) set a new record in 2004 with the fastest ascending speeds in the world. At 60.6 kilometres (37.7\xc2\xa0mi) per hour, 16.83\xc2\xa0m (55.22\xc2\xa0ft) per second, or 1010 m/min,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMD_34-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TMD-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the speed of Taipei 101\'s elevators is 34.7 percent faster than the previous record holders of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Yokohama_Landmark_Tower" title="Yokohama Landmark Tower">\n        Yokohama Landmark Tower\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Elevator" title="Elevator">\n        elevator\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">\n        Yokohama\n       </a>\n       , Japan, which reaches speeds of 12.5\xc2\xa0m (41\xc2\xa0ft) per second (45.0\xc2\xa0km/h, 28.0\xc2\xa0mi/h). Taipei 101\'s elevators sweep visitors from the fifth floor to the 89th-floor observatory in only 37 seconds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Each elevator features an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerodynamic" title="Aerodynamic">\n        aerodynamic\n       </a>\n       body, full\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressurization" title="Pressurization">\n        pressurization\n       </a>\n       , state-of-the art emergency braking systems, and the world\'s first triple-stage anti-overshooting system. The cost for each elevator is NT$80\xc2\xa0million (US$2.4\xc2\xa0million).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A 660-tonne (728-short-ton)\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuned_mass_damper" title="Tuned mass damper">\n        tuned mass damper\n       </a>\n       (TMD), located between the 87th and 91st floors,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMD_34-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TMD-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       stabilizes the tower against movements caused by high winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SnarkyNomad_2013_41-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SnarkyNomad_2013-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The damper can reduce up to 40 percent of the tower\'s movements.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The TMD is visible to all visitors on the 87th through 91st floors.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMD_34-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TMD-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Two restaurants have opened on the 85th floor: Diamond Tony\'s, which offers European-style seafood and steak, and Shin Yeh 101 (\xe6\xac\xa3\xe8\x91\x89), which offers Taiwanese-style cuisine. Occupying all of the 86th floor is Taiwanese restaurant Ding Xian 101.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Din_Tai_Fung" title="Din Tai Fung">\n        Din Tai Fung\n       </a>\n       , several international dining establishments and retail outlets also operate in the adjoining mall. The multi-story retail mall adjoining the tower is home to hundreds of fashionable stores, restaurants, clubs and other attractions. The mall\'s interior is modern in design even as it makes use of traditional elements. The curled\n       <i>\n        ruyi\n       </i>\n       symbol is a recurring\n       <a href="/wiki/Motif_(visual_arts)" title="Motif (visual arts)">\n        motif\n       </a>\n       inside the mall. Many features of the interior also observe\n       <i>\n        feng shui\n       </i>\n       traditions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FS_57-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FS-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Floor_directory">\n        Floor directory\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Floor directory">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The 101st floor is home to a private VIP club named Summit 101, according to the observatory brochure. Before 2014, no information about this club was ever made public.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2014, photos of the exclusive club were shown on TV for the first time. A Taipei Financial Center Corporation spokesman said that only foreign dignitaries, Hollywood film actors, and high spenders in the Taipei 101 Mall (over NT $1 million in purchases) had been invited to the VIP club.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Access to the 101st floor requires two elevator transfers on the 89th and 93rd floors, respectively. There is only one service elevator that facilitates access to the top 9 floors (93-101). The 101st floor is divided into three levels: 101F (lower), 101MF (mezzanine) and 101RF (roof). The VIP club exists on the lower level, while 101RF, a mechanical floor, provides access to the 60-metre tall spire, which has 24 levels (numbered R1 through R24) that can only be accessed via ladder.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 92nd through 100th floors are officially designated as communication floors, although it\'s unknown if there are any radio or TV stations currently broadcasting from the top of Taipei 101. The 91st-floor observatory is the highest floor that is open to the public, but unlike the leased/private floors from 7~90F, there is no sign of even a visible access point to the topmost floors on Level 91. The top 10 floors are to have stated on their website to contain a radio and television relay station, Emergency system receiving/signaling relay station, telecommunications stations, and an outdoor antenna frame on 96F, which offers power, fire protection, telecom systems, and security related systems, according to their website.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       4 is considered an\n       <a href="/wiki/Tetraphobia#In_China" title="Tetraphobia">\n        unlucky number\n       </a>\n       in Chinese culture,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FSnumber_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FSnumber-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       so what would have been the 44th floor has been replaced by Level 43, with 42A replacing the actual 43 to compensate for the skipped floor number.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is a freight elevator that facilitates access to every level from B5 to 91, with a button for every floor.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A tenant directory is posted in the first-floor lobby (from the Xinyi entrance.) As of 1 January 2011, the highest occupied office floor (excluding the observatory and restaurants) is 75. The building appears to be at least 70 percent occupied at this point. All publicly accessible floors have wheelchair accessibility support.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2067" data-file-width="4905" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg/600px-Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg/900px-Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg/1200px-Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg 2x" width="600"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tallest_buildings_in_Asia.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Taipei 101, fourth from left, compared with other tallest buildings in Asia.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         101st floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         92nd \xe2\x80\x93 100th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Communication\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         91st floor\n     59th \xe2\x80\x93 84th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         High Zone Office\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         59th \xe2\x80\x93 60th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Sky lobbies\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         35th \xe2\x80\x93 58th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Mid Zone Office\n        </td>\n <a href="#cite_note-Report13-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         35th \xe2\x80\x93 36th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Sky lobbies\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         35th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Amenities\n         <sup class="reference" \xe2\x80\x93 34th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Low Zone Office\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         B1st \xe2\x80\x93 5th floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Taipei 101 Mall\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report13_2-7">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Report13-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         B5th - B2nd floor\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Parking Levels\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report13_2-8">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Report13-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Observation_Deck">\n        Observation Deck\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Observation Deck">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;max-width:162px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:160px;max-width:160px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg/158px-Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg/237px-Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg/316px-Taipei_101_outdoor_observatory_MichaD_1.jpg 2x" width="158"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          On the 91F outdoor observatory at 391.8\xc2\xa0m (1,285\xc2\xa0ft).\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:160px;max-width:160px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="4176" data-file-width="2774" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg/158px-Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg/237px-Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg/316px-Taiwan_2009_Taipei_101_Shopping_Mall_Entrace_At_Night_FRD_8585.jpg 2x" width="158"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Art work outside the mall at night.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:160px;max-width:160px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei101.Park.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="674" data-file-width="800" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Taipei101.Park.jpg/158px-Taipei101.Park.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Taipei101.Park.jpg/237px-Taipei101.Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Taipei101.Park.jpg/316px-Taipei101.Park.jpg 2x" width="158"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Taipei 101\'s east park as seen from the Indoor Observatory at noon.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 features an Indoor\n       <a href="/wiki/Observation_deck" title="Observation deck">\n        Observation deck\n       </a>\n       (88th and 89th floor) and an Outdoor Observation deck (91st floor). Both offer 360-degree views and attract visitors from around the world. The Indoor Observatory stands 383.4\xc2\xa0m (1,258\xc2\xa0ft) above ground, offering a comfortable environment, large windows with UV protection, recorded voice tours in eight languages, and informative displays and special exhibits. Here one may view the skyscraper\'s main damper, which is the world\'s largest and heaviest visible damper, and buy food, drinks and gift items. Two more flights of stairs take visitors up to the Outdoor Observatory. The Outdoor Observatory, at 391.8\xc2\xa0m (1,285\xc2\xa0ft) above ground,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_3-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emporis-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is the second-highest observation deck ever provided in a skyscraper and the highest such platform in Taiwan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DIT_21-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DIT-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Indoor Observatory is open thirteen hours a day (9:00\xc2\xa0am\xe2\x80\x9310:00\xc2\xa0pm) throughout the week as well as on special occasions; the Outdoor Observatory is open during the same hours as weather permits. Tickets may be purchased on site in the shopping mall (5th floor) or in advance through the Observatory\'s website.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tickets cost NT$500 (US$17, as of 9 September 2013) and allow access to the 88th through 91st floors via high-speed elevator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Art">\n        Art\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Art">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Many works of art appear in and around Taipei 101. These include: German artist\n       <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Horn" title="Rebecca Horn">\n        Rebecca Horn\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        Dialogue between Yin and Yang\n       </i>\n       in 2002 (steel, iron), American artist\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Indiana" title="Robert Indiana">\n        Robert Indiana\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        1-0\n       </i>\n       in 2002 and\n       <i>\n        Love\n       </i>\n       in 2003 (aluminum), French artist\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Moscovici" title="Ariel Moscovici">\n        Ariel Moscovici\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <i>\n        Between Earth and Sky\n       </i>\n       in 2002 (rose de la claret granite), Taiwanese artist Chung Pu\'s\n       <i>\n        Global Circle\n       </i>\n       In 2002 (black granite, white marble), British artist Jill Watson\'s\n       <i>\n        City Composition\n       </i>\n       in 2002 (Bronze), and Taiwanese artist Kang Mu Hsiang\'s\n       <i>\n        Infinite Life\n       </i>\n       in 2013 (aluminum).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floor89PPM_28-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Floor89PPM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Moreover, the Indoor Observatory hosts a regular series of exhibitions. The artists represented have included Wu Ching (gold sculpture), Ping-huang Chang (traditional painting) and Po-lin Chi (aerial photography).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNewsletter_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eNewsletter-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">\n        Construction\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Construction">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg/200px-Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg/300px-Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg/400px-Xu_2003_005_Taipei_101.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="475" height="421" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg/200px-Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg/300px-Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg/400px-Forbys_Taipei_101.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Taipei 101 near the end of construction during 2003, showing the concrete tower at the top still incomplete. The height of the building was still 449.2 meters at the time.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Planning for Taipei 101 began in July 1997\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report13_2-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Report13-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       during\n       <a href="/wiki/Chen_Shui-bian" title="Chen Shui-bian">\n        Chen Shui-bian\n       </a>\n       \'s term as Taipei mayor. Talks between merchants and city government officials initially centered on a proposal for a 66-story tower to serve as an anchor for new development in Taipei\'s 101 business district. Planners were considering taking the new structure to a more ambitious height only after an expat suggested it, along with many of the other features used in the design of the building. It wasn\'t until the summer of 2001 that the city granted a license for the construction of a 101-story tower on the site. In the meantime, construction proceeded and the first tower column was erected in the summer of 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report13_2-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Report13-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_64-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A major\n       <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">\n        earthquake\n       </a>\n       took place in Taiwan during 31 March 2002 destroying a construction crane at the rooftop, which was at floor number 47. The crane fell down onto the Xinyi Road beneath the tower, crushing several vehicles and causing five deaths \xe2\x80\x93 two crane operators and three workers who were not properly harnessed. However, an inspection showed no structural damage to the building, and construction work was able to restart within a week.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SED_29-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SED-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101\'s roof was completed three years later on 1 July 2003.\n       <a href="/wiki/Ma_Ying-jeou" title="Ma Ying-jeou">\n        Ma Ying-jeou\n       </a>\n       , in his first term as Taipei mayor, fastened a golden bolt to signify the achievement.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_3-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emporis-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The formal opening of the tower took place on New Year\'s Eve 2004. President Chen Shui-bian, Taipei Mayor Ma Ying-jeou and Legislative Speaker\n       <a href="/wiki/Wang_Jin-pyng" title="Wang Jin-pyng">\n        Wang Jin-pyng\n       </a>\n       cut the ribbon. Open-air concerts featured a number of popular performers, including singers\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-Mei" title="A-Mei">\n        A-Mei\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Stefanie_Sun" title="Stefanie Sun">\n        Stefanie Sun\n       </a>\n       . Visitors rode the elevators to the Observatory for the first time. A few hours later the first fireworks show at Taipei 101 heralded the arrival of a new year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CP_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CP-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Chronology">\n        Chronology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Chronology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Important dates in the planning and construction of Taipei 101 include the following:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floor89PPM_28-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Floor89PPM-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table roof completed.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         17 October 2003\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Pinnacle placed.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n
