certifies Taipei 101 as world\'s tallest building.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         12 November 2004\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Tower obtains occupancy permit.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         31 December 2004\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Tower opens to the public.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report13_2-12">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Report13-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         1 January 2005\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         First New Year fireworks show begins at midnight.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Events">\n        Events\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Events">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg/170px-Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg/255px-Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg/340px-Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101-e%3Dmc2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence">\n          E=mc\n          <sup>\n           2\n          </sup>\n         </a>\n         lighting on 19 April 2005.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Taipei 101 is the site of many special events. Art exhibits, as noted above, regularly take place in the Observatory. A few noteworthy dates since the tower\'s opening include these.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 28 February 2005, Former President of the United States\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">\n        Bill Clinton\n       </a>\n       visited and signed copies of his autobiography.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clinton2005_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Clinton2005-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 19 April 2005, the tower displayed the formula "\n       <a href="/wiki/Mass%E2%80%93energy_equivalence" title="Mass\xe2\x80\x93energy equivalence">\n        E=mc\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n       </a>\n       " in lights to celebrate the 100th anniversary of the publication of\n       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">\n        Einstein\'s\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_relativity" title="Theory of relativity">\n        theory of relativity\n       </a>\n       . The display, the largest of 65,000 such displays in 47 countries, was part of the international celebration\n       <i>\n        Physics Enlightens the World.\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNewsletter_73-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eNewsletter-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 20 October 2006, the tower displayed a pink ribbon in lights to promote breast cancer awareness. The ten-day campaign was sponsored by Taipei 101\'s ownership and\n       <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A9e_Lauder_Companies" title="Est\xc3\xa9e Lauder Companies">\n        Est\xc3\xa9e Lauder\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNewsletter_73-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eNewsletter-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 25 December 2004, French\n       <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">\n        rock\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Buildering" title="Buildering">\n        urban climber\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Alain_Robert" title="Alain Robert">\n        Alain Robert\n       </a>\n       made an authorized climb to the top of the pinnacle in four hours.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 12 December 2007, Austrian\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Base_jumping" title="Base jumping">\n        base jumper\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Felix_Baumgartner" title="Felix Baumgartner">\n        Felix Baumgartner\n       </a>\n       survived an unauthorized parachute jump from the 91st floor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 20 November 2005, the First annual Taipei 101 Run Up featured a race up the 2,046 steps from floors 1 to 91. Proceeds were to benefit Taiwan\'s Olympic teams. The men\'s race was won by Paul Crake of Australia (10 minutes, 29 seconds), and the women\'s race by Andrea Mayr of Austria (12 minutes, 38 seconds).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eNewsletter_73-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-eNewsletter-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 15 June 2008, Taipei 101 Run Up featured 2,500 participants. The men\'s race was won by Thomas Dold of Germany (10 minutes, 53 seconds); 2007 champion\n       <a href="/wiki/Marco_De_Gasperi" title="Marco De Gasperi">\n        Marco De Gasperi\n       </a>\n       of Italy finished second and Chen Fu-tsai of Taiwan finished third. The women\'s race was won by Lee Hsiao-yu of Taiwan (14 minutes, 53 seconds).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="New_Year\'s_Eve_fireworks_displays">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_Year.27s_Eve_fireworks_displays">\n        New Year\'s Eve fireworks displays\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: New Year\'s Eve fireworks displays">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="867" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg/200px-Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg/300px-Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg/400px-Taipei_101_2008_NewYear_Firework.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taipei101fireworks.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="390" data-file-width="324" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Taipei101fireworks.jpg/200px-Taipei101fireworks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Taipei101fireworks.jpg/300px-Taipei101fireworks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/85/Taipei101fireworks.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="737" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg/200px-2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg/300px-2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg/400px-2008TaipeiCityNewYearCountdownParty_Firework_Taipei101_LoveTaiwan.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          New Year fireworks at Taipei 101, then show the "2008\n          <b>\n           \xe2\x99\xa5\n          </b>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TAIWAN" title="TAIWAN">\n           TAIWAN\n          </a>\n          " symbol Image.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The New Year\'s Eve show in Taipei is hosted at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taipei_City_Hall" title="Taipei City Hall">\n        Taipei City Hall\n       </a>\n       , which also provides a view of Taipei 101 which is lit up with fireworks. Another popular location for crowds to gather to see the fireworks display is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_Yat-sen_Memorial_Hall" title="Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall">\n        Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall\n       </a>\n       . For the first three years (2004\xe2\x80\x932006), the annual fireworks show at Taipei 101 was preceded by the sequential display of numerals in lights on each section to count down the last eight seconds to midnight. Since 2007 the building has been completely darkened, then fireworks begin to launch sequentially from the lower to upper sections.\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        2003\xe2\x80\x932004: Building still under construction. Spinning lights on the Outdoor Observatory (floor 91) provided a display of sound and lights, but no fireworks were launched.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2004\xe2\x80\x932005: Grand opening of Taipei 101 celebrated with the first fireworks display. The show lasted 35 seconds. Rockets were launched from section balconies. Festivities included all-day performances by popular entertainers and ceremonial visits by national dignitaries.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2005\xe2\x80\x932006: Show extended to 128 seconds.\n        <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">\n         Sony\n        </a>\n        sponsored the show, which concluded with a display of the brand name in lights.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2006\xe2\x80\x932007: Show extended to 188 seconds; 9,000 rockets were launched. This was Sony\'s second time sponsoring the event.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2007\xe2\x80\x932008: Show same length but featuring 12,000 rockets. Event Sponsor Taiwan Tourism Bureau ended the show with a display, in lights, of a heart over the word \'Taiwan\'.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2008\xe2\x80\x932009: A conspicuously more modest show than those which preceded it. The theme was "Love Taiwan With Your Heart In 2009". The show ended with the four sides of the building displaying lights in four colours (red, blue, green and yellow) to represent happiness, vision, sustainability and passion.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2009\xe2\x80\x932010: The display regained some of the dazzle of 2005\xe2\x80\x932008 shows but remained more brief in duration. The theme was "Taiwan Up."\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2010\xe2\x80\x932011: Show extended to 288 seconds (100 sec. for flash effects and 188 sec. for fireworks), and designed by\n        <a href="/wiki/Cai_Guo-Qiang" title="Cai Guo-Qiang">\n         Cai Guo-Qiang\n        </a>\n        , the artist also responsible for Beijing Olympics and World Expo Shanghai\'s fireworks. The theme was "100 ROC" (100th anniversary of the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">\n         Republic of China\n        </a>\n        ) which extended on the "Love Taiwan" theme. 2010 was also the year the Floral Expo was held in Taipei, and at Dajia Riverside Park there was another New Year\'s Eve event. It was a VIP event, but was broadcast simultaneously with the City Hall event. The display on the building was accompanied by fireworks going off other buildings in the Xinyi financial district. One concept was for fireworks to spiral up and down the building like\n        <a href="/wiki/Dragon" title="Dragon">\n         dragon\n        </a>\n        crawling, but technical difficulties caused some disappointment with what was anticipated (reported by the media to be more like "a worm"). It also took 30 seconds for the host to realize the fireworks were over.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2011\xe2\x80\x932012: The show was shortened to 202 seconds and was considered to be more conservative than that of the previous year, but featuring the largest number of rockets launched to date, totalling at 30,000. The theme coincided with the 101st anniversary of the ROC. It also gained attention on YouTube, where viewers noticed an apparent "\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFO" title="UFO">\n         UFO\n        </a>\n        " in the seconds before the fireworks started, later determined to be a radio-controlled glider with flashing lights.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2012\xe2\x80\x932013: The show was designed by the French pyrotechnics company Groupe F and was 198 seconds in length, featuring 22,000 rockets launched to an adaptation of Igor Stravinsky\'s\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_Firebird" title="The Firebird">\n          The Firebird\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        . The theme was "Swing for the Future." The words "Time for Taiwan" (both in English and Mandarin Chinese) were displayed in lights at the building to promote Taiwan Tourism Bureau\'s current advertising campaign.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2013\xe2\x80\x932014: The show lasted 218 seconds and a thematic music was created for the first time by local musicians to commemorate Taipei 101\'s 10th anniversary.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2014\xe2\x80\x932015: Marked 10th anniversary since the official opening on December 31, 2004. The show kept up to perform for 218 seconds. iSee Taiwan Foundation sponsored the fireworks to promote the beauty of Taiwanese culture and creativity. The firework music was arranged by Taiwanese Golden Melody award winner - Mr. Lee, Che-Yi, blended with the famous classical song The four seasons by Vivaldi and many Taiwanese folk music. Performed and recorded by Taipei Symphony Orchestra.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        2015\xe2\x80\x932016: It\'s the fourth time Group F designed the firework show for Taipei 101, with a green theme "Nature is Future" this year. The 238-second display was considered the longest performance ever. In addition to the most various and natural patterns of flowers, birds, seahorses, fishes, etc. were projected, 30,000 effects were one of the most to show. It\'s also the first time to have professional climbers to settle the firework racks onto the building fa\xc3\xa7ades. Mr. Lee, Chi-Yi once again arranged the music mixed with international and Taiwanese rhythms reflecting the nature-related theme and Evergreen Symphony Orchestra played the role of performance. A young Taiwanese IT design company BungBungame became the exclusive sponsor supporting a symbolic event showing Taiwan to the world.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Developments">\n        Developments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taipei_101&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Developments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Taipei Financial Center Corporation (TFCC) announced plans on 2 November 2009 to make Taipei 101 "the world\'s tallest green building" by summer of 2011 as measured by LEED standards. The structure is already designed to be energy-efficient, with double-pane windows blocking external heat by 50 percent and recycled water meeting 20\xe2\x80\x9330 percent of the building\'s needs. LEED certification would entail inspections and upgrades in wiring, water and lighting equipment at a cost of NT$60\xc2\xa0million (US$1.8\xc2\xa0million). Estimates show the savings resulting from the modifications would pay for the cost of making them within three years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-etaiwannews.com_82-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-etaiwannews.com-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The project was carried out under the guidance of an international team composed of\n       <a href="/wiki/Siemens_Building_Technologies" title="Siemens Building Technologies">\n        Siemens Building Technologies\n       </a>\n       , architect and interior designer Steven Leach Group and the LEED advisory firm EcoTech International.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http:.2F.2Fwww.buildingtechnologies.siemens.com.2Fbt.2Fglobal.2Fen.2FPages.2Fhome.aspx_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-http:.2F.2Fwww.buildingtechnologies.siemens.com.2Fbt.2Fglobal.2Fen.2FPages.2Fhome.aspx-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The company applied for a platinum-degree certification with LEED in early 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 28 July 2011, Taipei 101 received LEED platinum certification under "Existing Buildings: Operations and Maintenance". It displaced the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America_Tower_(Manhattan)" title="Bank of America Tower (Manhattan)">\n        Bank of America Tower\n       </a>\n       in Manhattan as the world\'s tallest and highest-use green building in addition to the Environmental Protection Agency building in Florida as the world\'s largest green building. Although the project cost NT$60 million (US$2.08 million), it is expected to save 14.4 million kilowatt-hours of electricity, or an 18 percent energy-saving, equivalent to NT$36 million (US$1.2 million) in energy costs each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FTleed_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FTleed-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2012, the shopping center at the base is expected to be remodeled.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n
